\newpage

Essentials for writing text are shown here. Demonstrations include creating a section and subsection, writing items in a bulleted list, citing items that are defined in `refs.bib`, and inserting R objects into the text.

# Section

A bulleted list:

- Results were produced with R version 4.2.3.[@r_language]

- Here's how to cite two or more things.[@orsf_aoas; @aorsf_joss; @aorsf_jcgs]

## Subsection

Here's how to put some results into the text: A total of 344 were included in the current analysis. The mean bill length was 44. The mean (standard deviation) body mass was 4,202 (802)

# References

In case they are needed.

<div id="refs"></div>

\newpage

# Tables

A convention worth following is to make each table a sub section. This makes the table easier to find from the table of contents and also from the built-in Rstudio navigator.



\newpage

<!-- new page not needed at the end of a block section -->

To make a landscape section, use the block_section code here. Note that the section will be applied to all content prior to the block reaching up to the most recent block.

```{=openxml}
<w:p><w:pPr><w:sectPr w:officer="true"><w:footerReference w:type="default"><w:ftr xmlns:wpc="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/word/2010/wordprocessingCanvas" xmlns:cx="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/drawing/2014/chartex" xmlns:cx1="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/drawing/2015/9/8/chartex" xmlns:cx2="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/drawing/2015/10/21/chartex" xmlns:cx3="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/drawing/2016/5/9/chartex" xmlns:r="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/officeDocument/2006/relationships" xmlns:w14="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/word/2010/wordml"><w:rPr/><w:fldChar w:fldCharType="begin" w:dirty="true"/></w:r><w:r xmlns:w="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/wordprocessingml/2006/main" xmlns:wp="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/wordprocessingDrawing" w:dirty="true">PAGE</w:instrText></w:r><w:r xmlns:w="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/wordprocessingml/2006/main" xmlns:wp="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/wordprocessingDrawing" w:dirty="true"/></w:r></w:p></w:ftr></w:footerReference><w:pgMar w:header="720" w:bottom="720" w:top="720" w:right="720" w:left="720" w:footer="720" w:gutter="720"/><w:pgSz w:h="11906" w:w="16838" w:orient="landscape"/><w:type w:val="continuous"/><w:cols/></w:sectPr></w:pPr></w:p>
```

To switch back to regular portrait section, add another portrait block. Notice how the block below acts on all content above it up to the prior block.

\newpage

# Figures

The default figure margins are set by the `page_long_above()` and `page_wide_above()`. You can change those to your preference by either modifying the functions or by setting `fig.width` and `fig.height` in the code chunk that prints the figure.

\newpage

## Figure 1: Penguin dimensions (normal version)


```{=openxml}
<w:p><w:pPr><w:jc w:val="center"/><w:pStyle w:val="Figure"/></w:pPr><w:r><w:rPr/><w:drawing xmlns:r="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/officeDocument/2006/relationships"><wp:inline distT="0" distB="0" distL="0" distR="0"><wp:extent cx="5486400" cy="3657600"/><wp:docPr id="" name="" descr=""/><wp:cNvGraphicFramePr><a:graphicFrameLocks xmlns:a="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/main" noChangeAspect="1"/></wp:cNvGraphicFramePr><a:graphic xmlns:a="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/main"><a:graphicData uri="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/picture"><pic:pic xmlns:pic="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/picture"><pic:nvPicPr><pic:cNvPr id="" name=""/><pic:cNvPicPr><a:picLocks noChangeAspect="1" noChangeArrowheads="1"/></pic:cNvPicPr></pic:nvPicPr><pic:blipFill><a:blip cstate="print" r:embed="C:\Users\bjaeger\AppData\Local\Temp\1\RtmpsHUFS4\file29210a706aa0.png"/><a:stretch><a:fillRect/></a:stretch></pic:blipFill><pic:spPr bwMode="auto"><a:xfrm><a:off x="0" y="0"/><a:ext cx="76200" cy="50800"/></a:xfrm><a:prstGeom prst="rect"><a:avLst/></a:prstGeom><a:noFill/></pic:spPr></pic:pic></a:graphicData></a:graphic></wp:inline></w:drawing></w:r></w:p>
```

There is a `theme_set()` command at the beginning of the document that sets our preferred `ggplot` theme. It aims to use the same font family and font size in the plots as is used in the text. I recommended changing the `ggplot` theming if you decide to use a different style for the word doc. If you want to just lightly modify the theme for specific plots, you can use the `theme()` function to add your flair. 


## Figure 2: Penguin dimensions (wide version)


```{=openxml}
<w:p><w:pPr><w:jc w:val="center"/><w:pStyle w:val="Figure"/></w:pPr><w:r><w:rPr/><w:drawing xmlns:r="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/officeDocument/2006/relationships"><wp:inline distT="0" distB="0" distL="0" distR="0"><wp:extent cx="10058400" cy="5486400"/><wp:docPr id="" name="" descr=""/><wp:cNvGraphicFramePr><a:graphicFrameLocks xmlns:a="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/main" noChangeAspect="1"/></wp:cNvGraphicFramePr><a:graphic xmlns:a="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/main"><a:graphicData uri="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/picture"><pic:pic xmlns:pic="http://schemas.openxmlformats.org/drawingml/2006/picture"><pic:nvPicPr><pic:cNvPr id="" name=""/><pic:cNvPicPr><a:picLocks noChangeAspect="1" noChangeArrowheads="1"/></pic:cNvPicPr></pic:nvPicPr><pic:blipFill><a:blip cstate="print" r:embed="C:\Users\bjaeger\AppData\Local\Temp\1\RtmpsHUFS4\file2921031c5afa.png"/><a:stretch><a:fillRect/></a:stretch></pic:blipFill><pic:spPr bwMode="auto"><a:xfrm><a:off x="0" y="0"/><a:ext cx="139700" cy="76200"/></a:xfrm><a:prstGeom prst="rect"><a:avLst/></a:prstGeom><a:noFill/></pic:spPr></pic:pic></a:graphicData></a:graphic></wp:inline></w:drawing></w:r></w:p>
```

Hang on, how did the figure size change? That is an intended side effect of `page_long_above()` and `page_wide_above()`. Notably, if you ever want to avoid this convenient side effect, you can override it by setting `fig.width = X` and `fig.height = Y` where X and Y are your preferred figure width and height, in inches.

```{=openxml}
<w:p><w:pPr><w:sectPr w:officer="true"><w:footerReference w:type="default"><w:ftr xmlns:wpc="http://schemas.microsoft.com/office/word/2010/wordprocessingCanvas"
```
